<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Anders Behring Breivik</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><b>Anders Behring Breivik</b> (<small>Norwegian pronunciation:Â </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Norwegian" title="Help:IPA for Norwegian">[ËÉnËÉÊ ËbeËrÉªÅ ËbrÉiviËk]</a></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pronunciation_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-pronunciation-6">[6]</a></sup> born 13 February 1979) is a Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Right-wing_terrorism" title="Right-wing terrorism">far-right terrorist</a> who committed the <a href="/wiki/2011_Norway_attacks" title="2011 Norway attacks">2011 Norway attacks</a>. On 22 July 2011 he killed eight people by detonating a <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">van bomb</a> amid the <a href="/wiki/Regjeringskvartalet" title="Regjeringskvartalet">Regjeringskvartalet</a> in <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, then shot dead 69 participants of a <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Youth_League_(Norway)" title="Workers' Youth League (Norway)">Workers' Youth League (AUF)</a> summer camp on the island of <a href="/wiki/Ut%C3%B8ya" title="UtÃ¸ya">UtÃ¸ya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_sane_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_sane-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> In August 2012 he was convicted of <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murder</a>, causing a fatal explosion, and <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the day of the attacks, Breivik electronically distributed a compendium of texts entitled <i>2083: A European Declaration of Independence</i>, describing his militant ideology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpost-islamophobia_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-jpost-islamophobia-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suspect_wanted_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-suspect_wanted-14">[14]</a></sup> In them, he lays out a worldview encompassing opposition to <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> and blaming <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminism</a> for creating a European "cultural suicide".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones20110727_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jones20110727-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The texts call Islam and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_Marxism" title="Cultural Marxism">Cultural Marxism</a> the enemy and advocate the deportation of all Muslims from Europe based on the model of the <a href="/wiki/Bene%C5%A1_decrees" title="BeneÅ¡ decrees">BeneÅ¡ decrees</a>, while also claiming that feminism exists to destroy European culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-praguepost_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-praguepost-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Breivik wrote that his main <a href="/wiki/Motive_(law)" title="Motive (law)">motive</a> for the atrocities was to <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">market</a> his manifesto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Two teams of court-appointed <a href="/wiki/Forensic_psychiatry" title="Forensic psychiatry">forensic psychiatrists</a> examined Breivik before <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Anders_Behring_Breivik" title="Trial of Anders Behring Breivik">his trial</a>. The first report diagnosed Breivik as having <a href="/wiki/Paranoid_schizophrenia" title="Paranoid schizophrenia">paranoid schizophrenia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> A second psychiatric evaluation was commissioned following widespread criticism of the first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The second evaluation was published a week before the trial; it concluded that Breivik was not psychotic during the attacks nor during the evaluation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC100412_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC100412-22">[22]</a></sup> He was instead diagnosed as having <a href="/wiki/Narcissistic_personality_disorder" title="Narcissistic personality disorder">narcissistic personality disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-narcissism_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-narcissism-23">[23]</a></sup> His trial began on 16 April 2012, with closing arguments made on 22 June 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClosingArg_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ClosingArg-24">[24]</a></sup> On 24 August 2012, <a href="/wiki/Oslo_District_Court" title="Oslo District Court">Oslo District Court</a> delivered its verdict, finding Breivik sane and guilty of murdering 77 people. He was sentenced to 21 years in prison, in a form of <a href="/wiki/Preventive_detention" title="Preventive detention">preventive detention</a> that required a minimum of 10 years incarceration and the possibility of one or more extensions for as long as he is deemed a danger to society. This is the <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment_in_Norway" title="Life imprisonment in Norway">maximum penalty in Norway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Breivik announced that he did not recognize the legitimacy of the court, and therefore did not accept its decision; he claims he "cannot" appeal because this would legitimize the authority of the Oslo District Court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_2_AS_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-TV_2_AS-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>While imprisoned, Breivik has identified himself as a <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">national socialist</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagen191115_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dagen191115-29">[29]</a></sup> saying he previously exploited <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counterjihad" title="Counterjihad">counterjihadist</a> rhetoric in order to protect <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_nationalism" title="Ethnic nationalism">ethno-nationalists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Expo14_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Expo14-30">[30]</a></sup> In 2015, he said that he has never personally identified as a Christian, and called his religion <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odinism" title="Odinism">Odinism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagen191115_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dagen191115-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogeneratedvl_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogeneratedvl-31">[31]</a></sup> In 2016, in a four-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_trial" title="Civil trial">civil trial</a> Breivik sued <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Correctional_Service" title="Norwegian Correctional Service">Norwegian Correctional Service</a>, over his solitary confinement and the general conditions of imprisonment. Breivik claimed that his solitary confinement violated his <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> and asserted that he had been subjected to degrading treatment. The verdict, in which the government was found to have breached Article 3 of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Convention" title="Human Rights Convention">Human Rights Convention</a>, was appealed;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrk-33">[33]</a></sup> a trial, in Court of Appeal, is scheduled to start on 10 January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bt.no_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-bt.no-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>His family name is Breivik, while Behring, his mother's maiden name, is his <a href="/wiki/Middle_name" title="Middle name">middle name</a> and not part of the family name. His family name comes from <i>Breivika</i> in <a href="/wiki/Hadsel" title="Hadsel">Hadsel</a>, and literally means "broad <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Vik_(disambiguation)" title="Vik (disambiguation)">vik</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_sane_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_sane-7">[7]</a></sup> or "broad bay".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nedre_silkestraa.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2653" data-file-width="3117" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Nedre_silkestraa.jpg/220px-Nedre_silkestraa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Nedre_silkestraa.jpg/330px-Nedre_silkestraa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Nedre_silkestraa.jpg/440px-Nedre_silkestraa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nedre_silkestraa.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Anders Behring Breivik grew up in the <a href="/wiki/East_End_and_West_End_of_Oslo" title="East End and West End of Oslo">West End of Oslo</a>. From 1982 to 1994 he lived with his mother in this apartment building in <a href="/wiki/Sk%C3%B8yen" title="SkÃ¸yen">SkÃ¸yen</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Breivik was born in Oslo on 13 February 1979,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mass-murder_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-mass-murder-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagensnavn1979_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dagensnavn1979-2">[2]</a></sup> the son of Wenche Behring (1946â2013), a nurse, and Jens David Breivik (born 1935), a <a href="/wiki/Sivil%C3%B8konom" title="SivilÃ¸konom">civil economist</a>, who worked as a <a href="/wiki/Diplomat" title="Diplomat">diplomat</a> for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Norway" title="List of diplomatic missions of Norway">Norwegian Embassy</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and later in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph.co.uk_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph.co.uk-36">[36]</a></sup> He spent the first year of his life in London until his parents divorced when he was a year old. His father, who later married a diplomat, fought for, but failed to achieve, custody. When Breivik was four, living in Fritzners gate in Oslo, two reports were filed expressing concern about his mental health, concluding that Anders ought to be removed from parental care.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mummy.27s_boy_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mummy.27s_boy-37">[37]</a></sup> One <a href="/wiki/Psychologist" title="Psychologist">psychologist</a> in one of the reports made a note of the boy's peculiar smile, suggesting it was not anchored in his emotions but was rather a deliberate response to his environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In another report by psychologists from Norway's centre for child and youth psychiatry (SSBU) concerns were raised about how his mother treated him: "She 'sexualised' the young Breivik, hit him, and frequently told him that she wished that he were dead." In the report Wenche Behring is described as "a woman with an extremely difficult upbringing, <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality structure</a> and an all-encompassing if only partially visible depression" who "projects her primitive aggressive and sexual fantasies onto him [Breivik]". The psychologist who wrote the report was later forbidden from giving evidence in court by Behring, who herself was excused from testifying on health grounds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik lived with his mother and his half sister in the <a href="/wiki/East_End_and_West_End_of_Oslo" title="East End and West End of Oslo">West End of Oslo</a> and regularly visited his father and stepmother in France, until they divorced when he was 12. His mother also remarried, to an officer in the Norwegian Army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mummy.27s_boy_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mummy.27s_boy-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik chose to be <a href="/wiki/Confirmation" title="Confirmation">confirmed</a> into the Lutheran <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Norway" title="Church of Norway">Church of Norway</a> at the age of 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Union_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Union-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his adolescence, Breivik's behaviour was described as having become rebellious. In his early teen years he was a prolific <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graffiti_artist" title="Graffiti artist">graffiti artist</a>, part of the <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> community in Oslo West. He took his graffiti much more seriously than his comrades did and was caught by the police on several occasions; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Child_Welfare_Services_(Norway)" title="Child Welfare Services (Norway)">Child Welfare Services</a> were notified once and he was fined on two occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagbladet_2012-04-03_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dagbladet_2012-04-03-44">[44]</a></sup> According to Breivik's mother, after he was caught spraying graffiti on walls in 1995, at the age of 16, and fined, his father stopped contact with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagbladet_2012-04-03_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dagbladet_2012-04-03-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> They have not been in contact since then.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The opposite view is claimed by Breivik's father, that it was his son who broke off contact with him and that he would always have welcomed Anders despite his destructive activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian_2012-04-13_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_2012-04-13-47">[47]</a></sup> At this age he also broke off contact with the hip hop community after he fell out with his best friend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since adolescence, Breivik had spent much time on weight training, and started using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anabolic_steroids" title="Anabolic steroids">anabolic steroids</a>. He cared a lot about his own looks and about appearing big and strong.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steroids_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steroids-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>Anders Breivik has criticised both of his parents for supporting the policies of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_Labour_Party" title="Norwegian Labour Party">Norwegian Labour Party</a>, and his mother for being, in his opinion, a moderate feminist. He wrote about his upbringing: "I do not approve of the [my] super-liberal, matriarchal upbringing as it completely lacked discipline and has contributed to feminising me to a certain degree."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="School">School</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: School">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Breivik attended Smestad Grammar School, Ris Junior High, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartvig_Nissens_Upper_Secondary_School" title="Hartvig Nissens Upper Secondary School">Hartvig Nissens Upper Secondary School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Commerce_School" title="Oslo Commerce School">Oslo Commerce School</a> (1995â98).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gunfar_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-gunfar-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> A former classmate has recalled that he was an intelligent student, physically stronger than others of the same age, who often took care of people who were bullied.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Adulthood">Adulthood</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Adulthood">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Breivik was exempt from <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> to <a href="/wiki/Military_service#Norway" title="Military service">military service</a> in the Norwegian Army and has no military training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Defence_Security_Department" title="Norwegian Defence Security Department">Norwegian Defence Security Department</a>, which conducts the <a href="/wiki/Vetting" title="Vetting">vetting</a> process, say he was deemed "unfit for service" at the mandatory conscript assessment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1997, at age 18, he lost 2 million <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">kroner</a> ($369,556)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollars_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-dollars-55">[55]</a></sup> in the stock market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-new_face_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-new_face-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the age of 21 Breivik was in the customer service department of an unnamed company, working with "people from all countries" and being "kind to everyone".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DN.se_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-DN.se-57">[57]</a></sup> A former co-worker described him as an "exceptional colleague",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and a close friend of his said he usually had a big <a href="/wiki/Egotism" title="Egotism">ego</a> and would be easily irritated by those of Middle Eastern or <a href="/wiki/South_Asian_ethnic_groups" title="South Asian ethnic groups">South Asian</a> origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarusian</a> opposition figure Mikhail Reshetnikov,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Anders Breivik underwent paramilitary training in a camp organised by retired <a href="/wiki/KGB" title="KGB">KGB</a> colonel Valery Lunev. According to Reshetnikov, Breivik visited Belarus three times and had lasting connections with the country. According to official data, Breivik visited Belarus only once, as a tourist in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Norwegian prosecuting authorities claim that Breivik went to Belarus to meet a woman he had met on a dating website. This woman later visited him in Oslo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his early twenties he underwent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmetic_surgery" title="Cosmetic surgery">cosmetic surgery</a>, according to friends, for his chin, nose and forehead, and was very satisfied with the result.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steroids_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Steroids-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning_terror_attacks">Planning terror attacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Planning terror attacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Breivik claims that in 2002 (at the age of 23) he started a nine-year-plan to finance the 2011 attacks, founding his own <a href="/wiki/Computer_programming" title="Computer programming">computer programming</a> business while working at the customer service company. He claims that his company grew to six employees and "several offshore bank accounts", and that he made his first million kroner at the age of 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardianBusiness_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianBusiness-63">[63]</a></sup> The company was later declared bankrupt and Breivik was reported for several breaches of the law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> He then moved back to his mother's home, according to himself to save money. The first set of psychiatrists who evaluated him said in their report his mental health deteriorated at this stage and he went into a state of withdrawal and isolation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> His declared assets in 2007 were about <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">NOK</a>Â 630,000. (<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>116,410<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollars_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-dollars-55">[55]</a></sup>), according to Norwegian tax authority figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DN.se_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-DN.se-57">[57]</a></sup> He claims that by 2008 he had about <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_krone" title="Norwegian krone">NOK</a>Â 2,000,000 (<a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>369,556<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollars_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-dollars-55">[55]</a></sup>) and nine credit cards giving him access to â¬26,000 in credit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardianBusiness_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianBusiness-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2009, he founded a farming company under the name "Breivik Geofarm",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessregister_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-businessregister-66">[66]</a></sup> described as a farming <a href="/wiki/Enkeltpersonforetak" title="Enkeltpersonforetak">sole proprietorship</a> set up to cultivate vegetables, melons, roots and <a href="/wiki/Tuber" title="Tuber">tubers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCProfile_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCProfile-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2009, he visited <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a> in an attempt to buy illegal weapons. He was unable to obtain a weapon there, and decided to get weapons through legal channels in Norway instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cz_po_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-cz_po-68">[68]</a></sup> He bought one semi-automatic 9Â mm <a href="/wiki/Glock" title="Glock">Glock 17 pistol</a> legally by demonstrating his membership in a pistol club in the police application for a gun license, and the semi-automatic <a href="/wiki/Ruger_Mini-14" title="Ruger Mini-14">Ruger Mini-14</a> rifle by possessing a hunting license.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DB-skyttertaushet_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-DB-skyttertaushet-69">[69]</a></sup> Breivik's manifesto included writings detailing how he played video games such as <i><a href="/wiki/World_of_Warcraft" title="World of Warcraft">World of Warcraft</a></i> to relax, and <i><a href="/wiki/Call_of_Duty:_Modern_Warfare_2" title="Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 2">Call of Duty: Modern Warfare 2</a></i> for "training-simulation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> He told a court in April 2012 that he trained for shooting using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holographic_device" title="Holographic device">holographic device</a> while playing <i>Call of Duty</i>. He claimed it helped him gain target acquisition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik had no declared income in 2009 and his assets amounted to 390,000 kroner ($72,063<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollars_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-dollars-55">[55]</a></sup>), according to Norwegian tax authority figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DN.se_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-DN.se-57">[57]</a></sup> He states that in January 2010 his funds were "depleting gradually". On 23 June 2011, a month before the attacks, he paid the outstanding amount on his nine credit cards so he could have access to funds during his preparations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GuardianBusiness_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianBusiness-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late June or early July 2011, he moved to a rural area south of <a href="/wiki/%C3%85sta" title="Ãsta">Ãsta</a> in <a href="/wiki/%C3%85mot" title="Ãmot">Ãmot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hedmark" title="Hedmark">Hedmark county</a>, about 140Â km (87Â mi) north-east of Oslo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG-perp_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-VG-perp-72">[72]</a></sup> the site of his farm. As he admits in his manifesto he used the company as a cover to legally obtain large amounts of artificial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertiliser" title="Fertiliser">fertiliser</a> and other chemicals for the manufacturing of <a href="/wiki/ANFO" title="ANFO">explosives</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG-perp_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-VG-perp-72">[72]</a></sup> A farming supplier sold Breivik's company six tonnes of fertiliser in May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters6tonnes_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters6tonnes-73">[73]</a></sup> The newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Verdens_Gang" title="Verdens Gang">Verdens Gang</a></i> reported that after Breivik bought a small quantity of an explosive primer from an online shop in Poland, his name was among 60 passed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_Security_Service_(Norway)" title="Police Security Service (Norway)">Police Security Service (PST)</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Customs_Service" title="Norwegian Customs Service">Norwegian Customs Service</a> as having used the store to buy products. Speaking to the newspaper, Jon Fitje of PST said the information they found gave no indication of anything suspicious. He sets the cost of the preparations for the attacks at â¬317,000 â "130,000 out of pocket and 187,500 euros in lost revenue over three years." [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>]<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DN.se_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-DN.se-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik's farmer neighbour described him as looking like a "city dweller, who wore expensive shirts and who knew nothing about rural ways". Breivik had also covered up the windows of his house. The owner of a local bar, who once worked as a profiler of passengers' body language at Oslo airport, said there was nothing unusual about Breivik, who was an occasional customer at the bar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_terror_attacks">2011 terror attacks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2011 terror attacks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Norway_attacks" title="2011 Norway attacks">2011 Norway attacks</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oslo_view_of_city.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="2103" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Oslo_view_of_city.jpg/220px-Oslo_view_of_city.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Oslo_view_of_city.jpg/330px-Oslo_view_of_city.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Oslo_view_of_city.jpg/440px-Oslo_view_of_city.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1694" data-file-width="3932" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg/220px-Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg/330px-Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg/440px-Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Day_after_Oslo_bombing-11.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Flowers laid in front of <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Cathedral" title="Oslo Cathedral">Oslo Cathedral</a> the day after the attacks</div>

</div>
<p>On 22 July 2011, Breivik bombed government buildings in Oslo, which resulted in eight deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-formal-indictment_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-formal-indictment-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within a few hours of the explosion he arrived at <a href="/wiki/Ut%C3%B8ya" title="UtÃ¸ya">UtÃ¸ya</a> island, the site of a camp for <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_Youth_League_(Norway)" title="Workers' Youth League (Norway)">Worker's Youth League</a>, posing as a police officer in order to take the ferry to the island, and then fired intermittently for more than one hour, killing 69<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABC_News-77_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_News-77-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extremist_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-extremist-77">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andresen_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andresen-78">[78]</a></sup> with one murder victim as young as 14 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-norpolice_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-norpolice-79">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrest">Arrest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Arrest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Emergency_Response_Unit_(Norway)" title="Emergency Response Unit (Norway)">public force counter-terrorism unit (based in Oslo)</a> arrived on the island and confronted him, he surrendered without resistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> After his arrest, he was held by armed police on the island, and interrogated throughout the night, before being moved to a holding cell in Oslo.</p>
<p>Breivik confessed and said the purpose of the attack was to save Norway and Western Europe from a Muslim takeover, and that the Labour Party had to "pay the price" for "letting down Norway and the Norwegian people."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk1_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrk1-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<p>After his arrest Breivik referred to himself as "the greatest monster since <a href="/wiki/Vidkun_Quisling" title="Vidkun Quisling">Quisling</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quisling_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-quisling-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Booking_and_preparations_for_trial">Booking and preparations for trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Booking and preparations for trial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On the way to his first jail meeting, Breivik's police escort was met with an angry crowd, some of whom shouted "burn in hell" or "traitor", while others used stronger words.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andresen_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-Andresen-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk1_83-1"><a href="#cite_note-nrk1-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 July 2011, Breivik was charged with violating paragraph 147a of the Norwegian criminal code,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruling2011-07-25_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ruling2011-07-25-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> "destabilising or destroying basic functions of society" and "creating serious fear in the population",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haaretz1_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz1-88">[88]</a></sup> both of which are acts of terrorism under Norwegian law. He was ordered held for eight weeks, the first four in solitary confinement, pending further court proceedings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ruling2011-07-25_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ruling2011-07-25-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suspect_hints_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-suspect_hints-89">[89]</a></sup> The custody was extended in subsequent hearings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The indictment was ready in early March 2012. The <a href="/wiki/Director_of_Public_Prosecutions#Norway" title="Director of Public Prosecutions">Director of Public Prosecutions</a> had initially decided to censor the document to the public, leaving out the names of the victims as well as details about their deaths. Due to the reactions, this decision was reversed shortly prior to its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On 30 March, the <a href="/wiki/Borgarting_Court_of_Appeal" title="Borgarting Court of Appeal">Borgarting Court of Appeal</a> announced that it had scheduled the expected appeal case for 15 January 2013. It would have been<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2016)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> conducted in the same specially constructed court room where the initial criminal case was tried.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik was kept at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ila_Prison" title="Ila Prison">Ila Prison</a> after arrest. There, he had at his disposal three prison cells: one where he could rest, sleep, and watch DVD movies or television, a second that was set up for him to use a PC without Internet connection, and a third with gym equipment. Only selected prison staff with special qualifications were allowed to work around him, and the prison management aimed to not let his presence as a high-security prisoner affect any of the other inmates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG2601_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-VG2601-93">[93]</a></sup> Subsequent to the January 2012 lifting of letters and visitors censorship for Breivik, he received several inquiries from private individuals,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> and he devoted his time to writing back to like-minded people. According to one of his attorneys, Breivik was curious to learn whether his manifesto has begun to take root in society. Breivik's attorneys, in consultation with Breivik, considered whether to have some of his interlocutors called as witnesses during the trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Several media, both Norwegian and international, have requested interviews with Breivik. The first such was cancelled by the prison administration following a background check of the journalist in question. A second interview was agreed to by Breivik, and the prison requested a background check to be done by the police in the country where the journalist is from. No information has been given about the media organisations in question.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Psychiatric_evaluation">Psychiatric evaluation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Psychiatric evaluation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Breivik underwent his first <a href="/wiki/Psychological_evaluation" title="Psychological evaluation">examination</a> by court-appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forensic_psychiatrists" title="Forensic psychiatrists">forensic psychiatrists</a> in 2011. The psychiatrists diagnosed him with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paranoid" title="Paranoid">paranoid</a> <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a>, concluding that he had developed the <a href="/wiki/Mental_disorder" title="Mental disorder">disorder</a> over time and was <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychotic</a> both when he carried out the attacks and during the observation. He was also diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">abuse of non-dependence-producing substances</a> antecedent of 22 July. The psychiatrists consequently found Breivik to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Criminally_insane" title="Criminally insane">criminally insane</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FORENSIC01_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FORENSIC01-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the report, Breivik displayed <a href="/wiki/Mood_congruence" title="Mood congruence">inappropriate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reduced_affect_display" title="Reduced affect display">blunted affect</a> and a severe <a href="/wiki/Empathy#Lack" title="Empathy">lack of empathy</a>. He spoke incoherently in <a href="/wiki/Neologism" title="Neologism">neologisms</a> and had acted <a href="/wiki/Compulsive_behavior" title="Compulsive behavior">compulsively</a> based on a universe of bizarre, <a href="/wiki/Grandiose_delusions" title="Grandiose delusions">grandiose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delusion" title="Delusion">delusional</a> thoughts. Breivik alluded to himself as the future <a href="/wiki/Regent" title="Regent">regent</a> of Norway, master of life and death, while calling himself "inordinately loving" and "Europe's most perfect <a href="/wiki/Knight" title="Knight">knight</a> since WWII". He was convinced that he was a warrior in a "low intensity civil war" and had been chosen to <a href="/wiki/Messiah_complex" title="Messiah complex">save his people</a>. Breivik described plans to carry out further "executions of categories A, B and C traitors" by the thousands, the psychiatrists included, and to organize Norwegians in reservations for the purpose of <a href="/wiki/Selective_breeding" title="Selective breeding">selective breeding</a>. Breivik believed himself to be the "knight <a href="/wiki/Justiciar" title="Justiciar">Justiciar</a> grand master" of a <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar_and_popular_culture" title="Knights Templar and popular culture">Templar</a> organisation. He was deemed to be suicidal and homicidal by the psychiatrists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FORENSIC01_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-FORENSIC01-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to his defence attorney, Breivik initially expressed surprise and felt insulted by the conclusions in the report. He later said "this provides new opportunities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>The outcome of Breivik's first competency evaluation was fiercely debated in Norway by mental health experts, over the court-appointed psychiatrists' opinion and the country's definition of criminal insanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph0401_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph0401-101">[101]</a></sup> An extended panel of experts from the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Board_of_Forensic_Medicine" title="Norwegian Board of Forensic Medicine">Norwegian Board of Forensic Medicine</a> reviewed the submitted report and approved it "with no significant remarks".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DRK01_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-DRK01-102">[102]</a></sup> News in the meantime emerged that the psychiatric medical staff in charge of treating prisoners at <a href="/wiki/Ila_Detention_and_Security_Prison" title="Ila Detention and Security Prison">Ila Detention and Security Prison</a> did not make any observations that suggested he suffered from either psychosis, depression or was suicidal. According to senior psychiatrist Randi Rosenqvist, who was commissioned by the prison to examine Breivik, he rather appeared to have <a href="/wiki/Personality_disorder" title="Personality disorder">personality disorders</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraph0401_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph0401-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG0601_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-VG0601-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Counsels representing families and victims filed requests that the court order a second opinion, while the prosecuting authority and Breivik's lawyer initially did not want new experts to be appointed. On 13 January 2012, after much public pressure, the Oslo District Court ordered a second expert panel to evaluate Breivik's mental state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> He initially refused to cooperate with new psychiatrists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> He later changed his mind and in late February a new period of psychiatric observation, this time using different methods than the first period, was begun.</p>
<p>If the original diagnosis had been upheld by the court, it would have meant that Anders Behring Breivik could not be sentenced to a prison term. The prosecution could instead have requested that he be detained in a <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">psychiatric</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Norway" title="List of hospitals in Norway">hospital</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Medical advice would then have determined whether or not the courts decided to release him at some later point. If considered a perpetual danger to society, Breivik could have been kept in confinement for life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> Shortly after the second period of pre-trial psychiatric observation was begun, the prosecution said it expected Breivik would be declared legally insane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sky20120303_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sky20120303-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Province20120302_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Province20120302-110">[110]</a></sup> On 10 April 2012, the second psychiatric evaluation was published with the conclusion that Breivik was not psychotic during the attacks and he was not psychotic during their evaluation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC100412_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC100412-22">[22]</a></sup> Instead, they diagnosed <a href="/wiki/Antisocial_personality_disorder" title="Antisocial personality disorder">antisocial personality disorder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Narcissistic_personality_disorder" title="Narcissistic personality disorder">narcissistic personality disorder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-narcissism_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-narcissism-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Breivik expressed hope at being declared sane in a letter sent to several Norwegian newspapers shortly before his trial, he wrote about the prospect of being sent to a psychiatric ward: "I must admit this is the worst thing that could have happened to me as it is the ultimate humiliation. To send a political activist to a mental hospital is more sadistic and evil than to kill him! It is a fate worse than death."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 June 2012, Professor of Psychiatry <a href="/wiki/Ulrik_Fredrik_Malt" title="Ulrik Fredrik Malt">Ulrik Fredrik Malt</a> testified in court as an expert witness, saying he found it unlikely that Breivik had schizophrenia. According to Malt, Breivik primarily suffered from <a href="/wiki/Asperger_syndrome" title="Asperger syndrome">Asperger syndrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourette_syndrome" title="Tourette syndrome">Tourette syndrome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narcissistic_personality_disorder" title="Narcissistic personality disorder">narcissistic personality disorder</a> and possibly <a href="/wiki/Paranoia" title="Paranoia">paranoid</a> <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychosis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Malt cited a number of factors in support of his diagnoses, including deviant behaviour as a child, extreme specialization in Breivik's study of weapons and bomb technology, strange facial expression, a remarkable way of talking, and an obsession with numbers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Eirik Johannesen disagreed, concluding that Breivik was lying and was not delusional or psychotic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Johannesen had observed and spoken to Breivik for more than 20 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-trial_hearing">Pre-trial hearing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Pre-trial hearing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In the pre-trial hearing, February 2012, Breivik read a prepared statement demanding to be released and treated as a hero for his "pre-emptive attack against traitors" accused of planning <a href="/wiki/Cultural_genocide" title="Cultural genocide">cultural genocide</a>. He said, "They are committing, or planning to commit, cultural destruction, including deconstruction of the Norwegian ethnic group and deconstruction of Norwegian culture. This is the same as ethnic cleansing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criminal_trial">Criminal trial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Criminal trial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Trial_of_Anders_Behring_Breivik" title="Trial of Anders Behring Breivik">Trial of Anders Behring Breivik</a></div>
<p>The criminal trial of Breivik began on 16 April 2012 in <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Courthouse" title="Oslo Courthouse">Oslo Courthouse</a> under the jurisdiction of <a href="/wiki/Oslo_District_Court" title="Oslo District Court">Oslo District Court</a>. The appointed prosecutors were <a href="/wiki/Inga_Bejer_Engh" title="Inga Bejer Engh">Inga Bejer Engh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Svein_Holden" title="Svein Holden">Svein Holden</a> with <a href="/wiki/Geir_Lippestad" title="Geir Lippestad">Geir Lippestad</a> serving as Breivik's lead counsel for the defence. Closing arguments were held on 22 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ClosingArg_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ClosingArg-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Court_verdict">Court verdict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Court verdict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 24 August 2012 Breivik was adjudged sane and sentenced to <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment_in_Norway" title="Life imprisonment in Norway">containment</a>âa special form of a prison sentence that can be extended indefinitely again and againâwith an approximate time frame of 21 years and a minimum time of 10 years, the maximum penalty in Norway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Breivik did not appeal and on September 8 media announced that the verdict was final.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TV_2_AS_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-TV_2_AS-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>The court said "many people share Breivik's <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">conspiracy theory</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Eurabia" title="Eurabia">Eurabia</a> theory. The court finds that very few people, however, share Breivik's idea that the alleged '<a href="/wiki/Islamization" title="Islamization">Islamisation</a>' should be fought with terror."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prison_life">Prison life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Prison life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Skien_fengsel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2980" data-file-width="1968" height="257" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Skien_fengsel.jpg/170px-Skien_fengsel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Skien_fengsel.jpg/255px-Skien_fengsel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Skien_fengsel.jpg/340px-Skien_fengsel.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Skien_fengsel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The entrance of Telemark Prison's affiliate in <a href="/wiki/Skien" title="Skien">Skien</a> in 2009.(The sign says "Corrections Service/ Skien Prison")</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Since August 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp2_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp2-122">[122]</a></sup> (and as of 2016) he is still imprisoned in a <i>SHS</i> section (a prison section with "particularly high security"â<i><b>s</b>Ã¦rlig <b>h</b>Ã¸y <b>s</b>ikkerhet</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Since the inception of <i>SHS</i> in 2002 - until 2016, Norway has only imprisoned ten or eleven<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> prisoners under <i>SHS</i> conditions, of which Breivik's term has been the longest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp12_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp12-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>He is imprisoned at Telemark Prison's affiliate in <a href="/wiki/Skien" title="Skien">Skien</a>. His previous prison transfers are: On 23 July 2012 he transferred from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ila_Prison" title="Ila Prison">Ila Prison &amp; Detention Center</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> to Telemark Prison's affiliate in Skien (100 kilometres (62Â mi) southwest of Oslo);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> on 28 September 2012 he transferred back; since September 2013 he has been back at Telemark Prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp2_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp2-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2015, Breivik has visits from a <a href="/wiki/Prison_visitor" title="Prison visitor">prison visitor</a> âa <a href="/wiki/Military_chaplain" title="Military chaplain">military chaplain</a> (ranked <a href="/wiki/Major" title="Major">major</a>) â every two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> His mother visited him five times before her death in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp3_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp3-130">[130]</a></sup> Researcher <a href="/wiki/Mattias_Gardell" title="Mattias Gardell">Mattias Gardell</a> interviewed Breivik in 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expressen1_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-expressen1-131">[131]</a></sup> No other visitors requested by Breivik have been granted access.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp3_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp3-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>He enrolled as a full student in the bachelor degree program in <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a> at the University of Oslo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik has converted to Nazism while in prison, according to his lawyer Ãystein Storrvik<a class="extiw" href="https://no.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%98ystein_Storrvik" title="no:Ãystein Storrvik">(no)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="De_facto_isolation_from_all_other_prisoners">De facto isolation from all other prisoners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: De facto isolation from all other prisoners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>He is isolated from the other inmates, and only has contact with health care workers and guards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewsComAu_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewsComAu-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>The type of isolation that Breivik has endured in prison, is what the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECtHR" title="ECtHR">ECtHR</a> calls <i><a href="/wiki/Solitary_confinement" title="Solitary confinement">relative social isolation</a></i>, according to a verdict of 2016 in <a href="/wiki/Oslo_District_Court" title="Oslo District Court">Oslo District Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp3_130-2"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp3-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Europe it is not uncommon to grant compensatory measures to prisoners that are being held in isolation for several years. As of 2016 he has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_typewriter" title="Electric typewriter">electric typewriter</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">Xbox</a> (without internet connection) in his cell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> (Previously, when the 2012 verdict was upheld in September 2012, permission for access to a computer (without internet) in his prison cell, ended. In November 2012 he received an electric typewriter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp3_130-3"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp3-130">[130]</a></sup>)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_activity_and_attempts_at_correspondence">Political activity and attempts at correspondence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Political activity and attempts at correspondence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012 Breivik planned to set up an organisation he called the <i>Conservative Revolutionary Movement</i> which he envisioned consisting of around 50 right-wing activists in Europe, as well as an organization for imprisoned right-wing activists; Breivik has written to, among others, <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Malm%C3%B6_shootings" title="2009â10 MalmÃ¶ shootings">Peter Mangs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beate_Zsch%C3%A4pe" title="Beate ZschÃ¤pe">Beate ZschÃ¤pe</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> media claimed in 2014 that Mangs had received letters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-expressen1_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-expressen1-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012 he spent 8â10 hours per day writing. He has said that he wants to write three books: the first being his own account of the events on the day of the attacks, the second discussing the ideology underlying his actions, and a third on his visions for the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG-20120726_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-VG-20120726-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Views_and_news_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Views_and_news-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>Politicians from several Norwegian parties have protested Breivik's activities in prison, which they see as him continuing to espouse his ideology and possibly encouraging further criminal acts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG-20120726_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-VG-20120726-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Views_and_news_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-Views_and_news-139">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Obstruction_of_postal_letters">Obstruction of postal letters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Obstruction of postal letters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since 2013 Breivik has been back at Telemark Prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verdictp2_122-2"><a href="#cite_note-Verdictp2-122">[122]</a></sup> After he came to Skien Prison, only 5 out of 300 letters that he had sent, had not been confiscated, he testified in court in 2016. He added, "Of the 200 forms regarding prison visits that I have mailed, all have been" confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>By 2016 around 4,000 postal items had been sent to or from Breivik, and about 15 percent of these (600 items) had been confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk.no_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-nrk.no-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 March 2016 political scientist Ingeborg Kjos received a letter from Breivik that had taken over a year and a half to reach her; the letter did not advocate violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans_for_hunger_strikes">Plans for hunger strikes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Plans for hunger strikes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In November 2012, Breivik wrote a 27-page letter of complaint to the prison authorities about the security restrictions he was being held under, claiming that the prison director personally wanted to punish him. Among his complaints were that his cell is not adequately heated and he has to wear three layers of clothing to stay warm, guards interfere with his strictly-planned daily schedule, his cell is poorly decorated and has no view, his reading lamp is inadequate, guards supervise him while he is brushing his teeth and shaving and put indirect mental pressure on him to finish quickly by tapping their feet while waiting, he is "not having candy" and he is served cold coffee, and he is strip-searched daily, sometimes by female guards. Authorities only lifted one minor restriction against Breivik; his rubber safety pen, which he described as an "almost indescribable manifestation of sadism," was replaced with an ordinary pen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>In letters to foreign media outlets he told about his demands (in 2013) to prison authorities "including easier communication with the outside world and a PlayStation 3 to replace the current PlayStation 2, because it offers more suitable games"; media reported in 2014 about demands that he would starve himself to death if refused "access to a sofa and a bigger gym"; furthermore he said that "Other inmates have access to adult games while I only have the right to play less interesting kidsâ games. One example is â<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rayman_Revolution" title="Rayman Revolution">Rayman Revolution</a>,â a game aimed at 3-year-olds," Breivik complained to prison officials."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LA_Times_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-LA_Times-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Star_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Star-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, Breivik again threatened a <a href="/wiki/Hunger_strike" title="Hunger strike">hunger strike</a>, because of deteriorating prison conditions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-132">[132]</a></sup> but delayed in order to sue the Norwegian Government over prison conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewsComAu_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-NewsComAu-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_trial_against_Norway.27s_government">Civil trial against Norway's government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Civil trial against Norway's government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During 15â18 March 2016 Breivik was the plaintiff in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_trial" title="Civil trial">civil trial</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Justice_and_Public_Security" title="Ministry of Justice and Public Security">Ministry of Justice and Public Security</a> was the defendant in court since the Correctional Service (that is being sued) is subordinate to the ministry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aftenposten.no_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-aftenposten.no-146">[146]</a></sup> The verdict was appealed;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-147">[147]</a></sup> in court of appeals a trial is scheduled for January 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik is suing the government over his solitary confinement, and his general conditions of imprisonment, including a claim of an excessive use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Handcuff" title="Handcuff">handcuffs</a>. Breivik claimed that his solitary confinement violates his human rights and asserted that he had been subjected to "degrading treatment, including hundreds of strip searches and frequent searches of his cell, including at night."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 March 2016 media said that Oslo District Court had again refused to allow the press to join a walk-through of Breivik's prison cell in the following week. The second request had included the suggestion that one person, with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gagging_order" title="Gagging order">gagging order</a> in place, could represent the entire press corps, while joining the walk-through.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 March media said that parts of the trial proceedings would be closed to the general public, according to a decision by Oslo District Court, that upheld its previous ruling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 March members of the court performed a walk-through of prison cells used by Breivik at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ila_Prison" title="Ila Prison">Ila Prison</a>; later the same week the members of the court inspected the prison facilities used by Breivik at Skien Prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>The trial started, on 15 March, when Oslo District Court convened inside Skien Prison. Upon arrival, after police removed his handcuffs, Breivik shook hands with his lawyers, thereafter faced <a href="/wiki/Courtroom" title="Courtroom">the gallery</a> and performed a <a href="/wiki/Nazi_salute" title="Nazi salute">Nazi-style salute</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> A lawyer from the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Attorney_General_of_Norway" title="Office of the Attorney General of Norway">Office of the Attorney General</a> said that of Breivik's incoming and outgoing mail, through the postal system, around 15 percent (or 600 pieces of mail out of around 4,000) had been confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk.no_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-nrk.no-141">[141]</a></sup> <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%98ystein_Storrvik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ãystein Storrvik (page does not exist)">Ãystein Storrvik</a>, the head of Breivik's legal team, told the court about Breivik's letter of complaint to the government in 2012 which detailed being awakened by flashlight as often as every half-hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Breivik.27s_testimony">Breivik's testimony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Breivik's testimony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 16 March Breivik started his testimony,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> "to give his view on the strict prison regimen [that he is exposed to] and any damage done to his health while in prison as a cause of isolation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aftenpostenvil_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-aftenpostenvil-156">[156]</a></sup> He reported having been handcuffed 3,500 times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-2"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The main points of his testimony were:</p>
<ul>
<li>He had been subjected to a "grip manoeuvre" 2,300 timesâwhere he put his hands through the slot of the door to his prison cell, and his hands had been held in place by a prison officer while the door has been swung open. Breivik described these two forms of "extra punishment", saying: "it is quite demeaning to be exposed to this every day, so I countered by not leaving my prison cell. I did not want to exercise in the fresh air, [I did not want to] train, or use my study [prison-] cell".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-3"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>On paper he had three prison cells, but because of the government's actions he hardly used the training cell and the study cell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-4"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Prison officers at Ila Prison were not to speak to him during his [first] stay there, and this was the case for parts of his stay at Skien [prison]; only the chief of the section was supposed to speak to Breivik. He said that he had not said "no" to the prison offering him activities such as playing <a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">floorball</a> or <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>, but asked to be offered other activities. He said that starting in March 2014 he finally received the one hour of fellowship with prison officers; he said that claims had been made that he was allowed to prepare food, but that he was permitted only to press an egg cooker, and was not permitted to put frozen <a href="/wiki/Pizza" title="Pizza">pizza</a> in the ovenâthat he had only done once.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-5"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>He still received a <a href="/wiki/Prison_visitor" title="Prison visitor">prison visitor</a> twice a monthâan officer of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Armed_Forces" title="Norwegian Armed Forces">Norwegian Armed Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-6"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Regarding recreation in fresh air, Breivik said: "Until December 2015 all outdoors recreation was in a concrete box. In December 2015, probably because of the upcoming trial, I was permitted to walk 20 minutes in the outdoors recreation area. A couple of times later I was permitted [again]. Thereafter I was permitted to recreate there every other week".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-7"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Regarding being awoken at night, Breivik said: "There are inspections through the slot [of the door to the prison cell] every 40 minutes. Every time the slot was opened they demanded a sign of life. They wanted me to shake a leg every time the slot opened". He felt humiliated that the prison officers made such demand and said "They shined a flashlight into the bed, depending on the prison officer. Called into the cell <i>Are you alive, are you alive</i>, until I woke up. Then they had the sign of life that they needed. Countless times I was awoken at night".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-8"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>After he came to Skien Prison, only 5 out of 300 letters that Breivik sent, had not been confiscated. He added, "Of the 200 forms regarding prison visits that I have mailed, all have been" confiscated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-9"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2015 he was told that he would be locked into an isolation cell for 23 hours a day; the decision was reversed in December 2015, weeks after the visit by the <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Ombudsman" title="Parliamentary Ombudsman">Parliamentary Ombudsman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-10"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik talked about the parties NFP and NL, that he said later changed name to "<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nordic_State&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nordic State (page does not exist)">Nordic State</a>" (<i>Nordiske stat</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-11"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik said that "Dark film on all the windows has prevented natural light, and it is not possible to see anything outside during large parts of the winter months of the year ".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-12"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik testified about how the authorities prevent him from buying postage stamps, and how Skien Prison has confiscated envelopes [where the stamps are] worth several thousand <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_kroner" title="Norwegian kroner">Norwegian kroner</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-13"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik told about having to wait a long time after having asked for [the prison officers to present his] toothbrush, or asked [the prison officers] about turning off the TV switch; "This low-level terrorising continued for two years until" his transfer to Skien [prison].<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-14"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik testified that he had to drink cold coffee because he was not permitted to have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermos" title="Thermos">thermos</a>; Breivik has also complained about announcements over the PA system at Ila, including that each message was repeated such as <i>Now it's time for outdoors recreation, it's time for outdoors recreation</i>; the PA system was eventually switched off in Breivik's section [at the prison].<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-15"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik said that "The reservoir of strength that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_socialism" title="National socialism">national socialism</a> has given me, was finished in December".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-16"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik testified that after two years in isolation he has started to love <a href="/wiki/Paradise_Hotel" title="Paradise Hotel">Paradise Hotel</a>, which he says is evidence that he has become seriously brain damaged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-17"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik says that he had not been permitted to publish his correct mailing address.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-18"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik said that "It is important that Oslo District Court says what types of addressees [pertaining to the postal system] are permissible". He added that media [outlets] that he has access to are <i><a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">Aftenposten</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dagen_(Norwegian_newspaper)" title="Dagen (Norwegian newspaper)">Dagen</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Telemarksavisa" title="Telemarksavisa">TA</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Varden_(newspaper)" title="Varden (newspaper)">Varden</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Teletext" title="Teletext">broadcast Teletext</a> on several channels; he would read other newspapers if he had such access, "<a href="/wiki/Klassekampen" title="Klassekampen">Klassekampen</a> is perhaps even more interesting than Aftenposten".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-19"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></li>
<li>Breivik said that "Isolation is the most effective way to radicalise people because one never gets corrected by others".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cross-examination_of_witnesses">Cross-examination of witnesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Cross-examination of witnesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The first witness, Randi Rosenqvist, a psychiatrist at Ila Prison, was cross-examined by Storrvik.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-20"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Storrvik asked if she had suggested visits without a glass wall; Rosenqvist replied: "Yes I have discussed this. I have been thinking that visits without a glass wall could be something [to consider]. I don't think that with his image, he would be violent to someone he has [some sort of] a [working-] relationship to". Storrvik read out loud, recommendations by Rosenqvist, including "Retired police officers could, for example, come [to socialise with Breivik], drink coffee, play games".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-21"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/NRK" title="NRK">NRK</a> reported that "The <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Ombudsman" title="Parliamentary Ombudsman">Parliamentary Ombudsman</a> has previously reported that the regimen for serving a prison sentence at the level of <i>particularly high security</i>" constitutes a heightened risk of inhumane treatment. Now it appears that Parliamentary Ombudsman will not testify".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-22"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> This was despite the fact that one of its leaders was on the list of witnesses summoned to testify.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_149-2"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the start of the third day of the trial, Storrvik introduced a report from the "prevention section" at [the office of] the Parliamentary Ombudsman, dated 11 November 2015, regarding a series of visits that year by the ombudsman; the report said that Breivik was being held at a section where sometimes there was only one prisoner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-23"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Storrvik read from the report that "The limitations on visits at the time of the inspection [by the Parliamentary Ombudsman] seemed quite strict". He said that in that section of the prison, it should expand the planned community between prisoners and employees and consider other measures to minimise the risk of isolation damage. At that section the prison should evaluate alternative possibilities for recreation in fresh air, in addition to the concrete exercise yard. The report recommended that the prison should discontinue the visual surveillance of health-related conversations that occur with a glass wall between prisoner and health personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-24"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
