<p>The second witness was Knut Bjarkeid, <a href="/wiki/Superintendent_(jail)" title="Superintendent (jail)">Chief Warden</a> at Ila Prison. Storrvik confronted Bjarkeid with a document regarding [prison] Section G being turned [in part] into a "particularly high security department". He read: "There are obvious limits to how long he can be in Section G"; the document was written by Bjarkeid. Storrvik said that "The words are here, obviously there are limits to how long he shall be isolated. This was in 2012. He is still in total isolation". After Bjarkeid left the witness stand, Emberland read out loud from a letter that Breivik had written, dated 29 September 2013; in the letter Breivik reported several persons to the police; the <a href="/wiki/Asker" title="Asker">Asker</a> and <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A6rum" title="BÃ¦rum">BÃ¦rum</a> Police District investigated and later dropped the investigation; Breivik's letter detailed the number of <a href="/wiki/Strip_search" title="Strip search">strip searches</a>, "grip manoeuvres", and handcuffings he had undergone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-25"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The third witness was BjÃ¸rn Draugedalen, a <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">general practitioner</a> working one day per week at Skien Prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-26"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> His first consultation with Breivik was held in a <a href="/wiki/Recreation_room" title="Recreation room">recreation room</a> in <i>avdeling for sÃ¦rlig hÃ¸y sikkerhet</i>, a high-security unit. Draugedalen shook hands with Breivik, with five prison officers present; all the later consultations (until the trial) were held with a glass wall separating them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-27"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Storrvik asked "This change, when another prisoner arrived [and started to live in the same prison section], which resulted in Breivik's movement being restrictedâdid you consider to go up there to view [his living conditions or] how things were"?; Draugedalen answered "We have to deal with changes done by the Corrections Services".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-28"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> The judge interjected, and she said that the Correction Services likely would listen to health care workers; Draugedalen replied that "We did not see any extra value then, regarding visiting him in the [prison] section".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-29"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> At 12:36 Draugedalen said that he has not been notified that Breivik has discontinued his [college/university] studies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-30"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fourth witness was Haukeland, an MD for prisoners at Ila Prison. At 13:46 Storrvik read from [Breivik's medical] record dated 5 February 2013 that Breivik intends to recreate less in fresh air because of the strip searches that follow; Storrvik asked Haukeland: "The fact that he goes outside less, to avoid being strip searched, was that discussed as a problem?; Haukeland answered "No, that was not discussed [among the health care workers or] in the health section".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-31"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> At 13:51 the judge referred to nightly inspections every half hour, and Haukeland answers that he cannot remember; the judge asked "Were you the ones who recommended that"?; Haukeland replied "No (...)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-32"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The fifth witness was Margit Kise, a section leader at Skien Prison, who served from September 2013 to May 2015 in section A and H. The sixth witness was Tore Stenshagen, also a section leader at Skien, who served during the third quarter of 2015. Stenshagen testified that sometimes he sits down [in Breivik's cell] and talks with Breivik, and sometimes they are accompanied by only one prison officer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-33"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>The seventh witness was JÃ¸rgen Spangen Iversen, an advisor at the Correctional Agency. Iversen was asked why Breivik was transferred to Skien rather than to <a href="/wiki/Ringerike_Prison" title="Ringerike Prison">Ringerike Prison</a>; Iversen answered that he became a case-worker in 2014, and he was not involved in the transfer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-34"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Closing_arguments">Closing arguments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Closing arguments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Summing up the case for Breivik, Storrvik said: "For some reason, in Norway it has been established that in a female prison, a male prison officer cannot strip search a prisoner, but in a male prison it is ok that females are present. This is offensiveâI do not see any alternatives".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-35"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> He then talked about the case of strip searches of prisoner Piechowicz<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-36"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> In that case the court was not convinced by the Polish government's arguments that the systematic, humiliating, daily searches were necessary to secure the prison. He continued: "He was also awoken at night, but he had 147 visits that compensated", and Piechowicz's isolation lasted for a shorter period; Storrvik said "Note that one calls it <i>isolation</i>, even though he had one cellmate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-37"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Storrvik said that "the verdict [of] Piechowicz vs. Poland point to a breach of <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">EMK</a> in our case".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-38"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Storrvik said "In my opinion there is not a complete concurrence between risk analyses and measures in our case. Risk analyses have at an early stage come with suggestions for measures [and these have not been followed up] (...) For example, removing the glass wall during visits and the possibility of introducing fellow prisoner, has been discussed at such an early stage that there should be a good reason for why Rosenqvist's advice has not been followed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-39"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Storrvik said that "The main problem for the government in this case is that the discrepancies between well-foundedâin the context of securityâsuggestions from one of those who knows this case the best has not been followed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saksoker2_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-saksoker2-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<p>Storrvik compared Breivik's position as a <a href="/wiki/Catch-22" title="Catch-22">Catch-22</a> situation: If Breivik says that he has psychiatric problems, then he has picked them out of a book; if he says that he doesn't have psychiatric problems, then he doesn't have psychiatric problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-40"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Storrvik said that there had been no inspections by agencies tasked with <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers" title="Separation of powers">oversight</a>, as far as he knew, until the Parliamentary Ombudsman came.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-41"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup> Breivik's lawyer referred to anal inspections [â<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_orifices" title="Natural orifices">visual or manual body cavity searches</a>]; he disagreed with Emberland's view that there was a difference regarding <i>anal inspection</i> as referred to in ECHR verdicts in other cases, and the squats that Breivik must perform while naked; Storrvik's opinion is that Ila lacks concrete reasons for all the inspections.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sksoker_129-42"><a href="#cite_note-sksoker-129">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mestad said that "The government's primary task is to protect its citizens. To let a convicted terrorist establish a network, is dangerous".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Veisende_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-Veisende-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<p>Storrvik said Breivik's [previous] verdict "indicates a mental vulnerability. If that is not enough, Breivik appearsâby my standardsâconfused in court".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ettkort_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ettkort-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Storrvik added that [in his usage] "<i>mental vulnerability</i> is a very, very <a href="/wiki/Understatement" title="Understatement">weak expression</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ettkort_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ettkort-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Emberland said that "Storrvik is quoting from the dissenting opinions from verdicts of the ECHR"âat least as much as he is quoting the majority opinions of the verdicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ettkort_162-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ettkort-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 March 2016 after the court was adjourned, the room where the trial had been held was turned back into the prison gymnasium.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_.28out_of_court.29_to_Breivik.27s_testimony">Reactions (out of court) to Breivik's testimony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Reactions (out of court) to Breivik's testimony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Breivik's testimony about his ideology was described as incoherent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Dagbladet" title="Dagbladet">Dagbladet</a>, Aina Sundt Gullhaugen (research advisor and psychologist) said about prison superintendent Bjarkeid's opinion that Breivik is not one of the prisoners at Ila suffering [from isolation]: "And surely it is an ugly sight when humans in the basement at Ila smear feces on the walls and no longer are oriented about themselves, time or place. But those who think that Breivik is not suffering have made themselves unavailable for the documented pain that Anders partook in [during childhood] ... The problem is that Breivik ... expresses his affliction in a manner that does not get captured particularly well by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Diagnostics_manual&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Diagnostics manual (page does not exist)">diagnostics manuals</a>. The type of fundamental relational and emotional deficiencies that Breivik was allowed to develop, usually results in that person ending up speaking a language that others don't recognise".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">Aftenposten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulrik_Fredrik_Malt" title="Ulrik Fredrik Malt">Ulrik Fredrik Malt</a> [expert witness at the 2012 trial] said that "the mass murderer is mentally quite ill, and that's being undercommunicated".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Verdict">Verdict</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Verdict">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 20 April 2016 District Court Judge Helen AndenÃ¦s Sekulic handed down her verdict.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The verdict said that the conditions of his imprisonment breached Article 3 of the <a href="/wiki/European_Convention_on_Human_Rights" title="European Convention on Human Rights">European Convention on Human Rights</a>, but that Article 8 of the Convention had not been violatedâconfiscation of letters had been justified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-nrk-33">[33]</a></sup> The government was also ordered to pay <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_kroner" title="Norwegian kroner">Norwegian kroner</a> 330,937.5 ($40,373)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk_33-2"><a href="#cite_note-nrk-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dollars2_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-dollars2-167">[167]</a></sup> for the plaintiff's legal expenses incurred by the court case. (Breivik could not receive the money, but his lawyer could upon the verdict being upheld.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Breivik was not in any courtroom when he received the verdict; media said that his copy would be faxed [to the prison].<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>"The verdict lists ... points regarding the breach of human rights:</p>
<ul>
<li>Length of isolation</li>
<li>Incomplete justification for the measure</li>
<li>Limited venues for complaints</li>
<li>Few compensating measures</li>
<li>Breivik's health condition was not taken into adequate consideration when the regimen of imprisonment was laid down.</li>
<li>The routine <a href="/wiki/Strip_search" title="Strip search">strip searches</a> Breivik had to endure after outdoors recreation, and the unannounced searches were not adequately justified from a security point of view".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nrk_33-3"><a href="#cite_note-nrk-33">[33]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The verdict said that "the prohibition against inhuman and degrading treatment represents a fundamental value in a democratic society. It applies no matter whatâeven when dealing with terrorists and killers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<p>The verdict highlighted the case of "van der Ven v. The Netherlands" (at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECtHR" title="ECtHR">ECtHR</a>) in 2003, saying that some of the regular strip searches lacked justification in Breivik's case also.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions_to_verdict_and_appeal">Reactions to verdict and appeal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Reactions to verdict and appeal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On 21 April 2016 news media said that Ole Kristoffer Borhaug (the <i>fengselsleder</i> at Telemark Prison of which Skien Prison is an affiliate) said that the prison regimen for Breivik would not be lightened, in part because the verdict has not been officially upheld, and there are regulations preventing high security prisoners from interacting with prisoners of other categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other reactions to the verdict include those of former convicts: <a href="/wiki/Kjell_Alrich_Schumann" title="Kjell Alrich Schumann">Kjell Alrich Schumann</a> said that the verdict is most importantly about the principles regarding the application of isolation in Norwegian prisons; he added that "The decisions are evaluated by an entity at Correctional Service every six months, and they can use any kinds of arguments. There is no oversight"; <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sven-Eirik_Utsi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sven-Eirik Utsi (page does not exist)">Sven-Eirik Utsi</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">Â (<a class="extiw" href="https://no.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sven-Eirik_Utsi" title="no:Sven-Eirik Utsi">no</a>)</span> said that "One can say whatever one wants about Breivik ... but isolation [is something] Norway has been criticised about for several decades [by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECtHR" title="ECtHR">ECtHR</a>]".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government's chief lawyer in the trial, Marius Emberland, had voiced his opinion about the verdict before the appeal; his opinion was criticized by the leader of the Norwegian Judges' Association, Ingjerd Thune:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> "I clearly understand that many react. I have never heard a lawyer speak in that mannerâever. That was surprising"; lawyer <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Frode_Sulland&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Frode Sulland (page does not exist)">Frode Sulland</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">Â (<a class="extiw" href="https://no.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frode_Sulland" title="no:Frode Sulland">no</a>)</span> said that one gets the impression that <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Attorney_General_of_Norway" title="Office of the Attorney General of Norway">Office of the Attorney General</a> "does not respect the justice system, and they still think that they are right, even when the court thinks they are wrong"; Emberland eventually recognised that some of his verbal comments can be interpreted as arrogant, adding that "They really weren't meant that way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 May media said that the government had handed in its ["appeal declaration"] <i>ankeerklÃ¦ring</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> previously the government had announced that it would appeal, including the part of the verdict that deals with reimbursing the costs of Breivik's legal aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aftenposten1_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-aftenposten1-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Legal scholar <a href="/wiki/Mads_Anden%C3%A6s" title="Mads AndenÃ¦s">Mads AndenÃ¦s</a>, said that "The appeal has no bearing on the responsibility of the government to evaluate and make the changes that the verdict of Oslo District Court imposes the government to do. This results directly from <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Norwegian_Law&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Norwegian Law (page does not exist)">Norwegian Law</a> and practices of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ECtHR" title="ECtHR">ECtHR</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C3.85dnehussandnes_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-.C3.85dnehussandnes-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>Regarding the question of [possibly] moving Breivik to a prison with other <i>SHS</i>-prisoners, Telemark Prison's director, Ole Kristoffer Borhaug, said that the question is the responsibility of the Correctional Service's "Region South".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.C3.85dnehussandnes_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-.C3.85dnehussandnes-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 August media said that Storrvik claims that the judge [scheduled to rule in the trial] is partial;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> the judge was recused.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> The trial is scheduled to start 10 January 2017;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bt.no_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-bt.no-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> one earlier date was rejected by Breivik's lawyer, Storrvik.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> The appeal was originally scheduled to be heard, over four days in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Borgarting_lagmannsrett" title="Borgarting lagmannsrett">Borgarting lagmannsrett</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financing_of_legal_aid.3B_family_situation">Financing of legal aid; family situation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Financing of legal aid; family situation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of 2016 Breivik is still receiving <a href="/wiki/Pro_bono" title="Pro bono">pro bono</a> <a href="/wiki/Legal_aid" title="Legal aid">legal aid</a> from the lawfirm of Ãystein Storrvik;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aftenposten1_177-1"><a href="#cite_note-aftenposten1-177">[177]</a></sup> previously the firm of <a href="/wiki/Geir_Lippestad" title="Geir Lippestad">Geir Lippestad</a> did <a href="/wiki/Pro_bono" title="Pro bono">pro bono</a> representation of Breivik (after the 2012 trial).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> Legal aid during criminal trials has been paid by the government, as is the norm in the country.</p>
<p>On 23 March 2013, Breivik's mother died from complications from cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> On the same day media said that mother and son "took farewell during a meeting at <a href="/wiki/Ila_Detention_and_Security_Prison" title="Ila Detention and Security Prison">Ila</a> last week. Breivik was permitted to move himself out from behind the glass wall of the visit roomâto give his mother a farewell hug".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Breivik had asked for permission by the prison officials to attend his mother's funeral service;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> the request was rejected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writings_and_video">Writings and video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Writings and video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forums">Forums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Forums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Janne_Kristiansen" title="Janne Kristiansen">Janne Kristiansen</a>, then Chief of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_Security_Service_(Norway)" title="Police Security Service (Norway)">Norwegian Police Security Service</a> (PST), said Breivik "deliberately desisted from violent exhortations on the net [and] has more or less been a moderate, and has neither been part of any extremist network."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> He is reported to have written many posts on the <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Islam" title="Criticism of Islam">Islam-critical</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> website <a href="/wiki/Document.no" title="Document.no">document.no</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRK_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRK-191">[191]</a></sup> He also attended a meeting of "Documents venner" (Friends of Document), affiliated with the website, in late 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Due to the media attention on his Internet activity following the 2011 attacks, <a href="/wiki/Document.no" title="Document.no">document.no</a> compiled a complete list of comments made by Breivik on its website between September 2009 and June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>A <i><a href="/wiki/Dagens_N%C3%A6ringsliv" title="Dagens NÃ¦ringsliv">Dagens NÃ¦ringsliv</a></i> article said that Breivik sought to start a Norwegian version of the <a href="/wiki/Tea_Party_movement" title="Tea Party movement">Tea Party movement</a> in cooperation with the owners of document.no, but that they, after expressing initial interest, turned down his proposal because he did not have the contacts he promised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="YouTube_video">YouTube video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: YouTube video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Six hours before the attacks, Breivik posted a picture of himself as a Knight Templar officer in a uniform festooned with a gold <a href="/wiki/Aiguillette" title="Aiguillette">aiguillette</a> and multiple medals he had not been awarded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> In the video he put an animation depicting Islam as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trojan_horse" title="Trojan horse">trojan horse</a> in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Analysts describe it as promoting physical violence towards Muslims and Marxists who reside in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Compendium">Compendium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Compendium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Content">Content</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Content">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Breivik prepared a document titled <i>2083: A European Declaration of Independence</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-link_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-link-199">[199]</a></sup> It has 1,518 pages, credited to "Andrew Berwick".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> Breivik admitted in court that it was mostly other people's writings he had copy pasted from different websites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cut-and-paste_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-cut-and-paste-202">[202]</a></sup> The file was e-mailed to 1,003 addresses about 90 minutes before the bomb blast in Oslo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-link_199-1"><a href="#cite_note-link-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The document describes two years of preparation of unspecified attacks, supposedly planned for late 2011, involving a rented <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Crafter" title="Volkswagen Crafter">Volkswagen Crafter</a> van (small enough not to require a truck driving licence) loaded with 1,160 kilograms (2,560Â lb) of <a href="/wiki/ANFO" title="ANFO">ammonium nitrate/fuel oil explosive (ANFO)</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ruger_Mini-14" title="Ruger Mini-14">Ruger Mini-14</a> <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_rifle" title="Semi-automatic rifle">semi-automatic rifle</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Glock#9x19mm_Parabellum" title="Glock">Glock 34 pistol</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personal_armour" title="Personal armour">personal armour</a> including a <a href="/wiki/Shield" title="Shield">shield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caltrop" title="Caltrop">caltrops</a>, and police <a href="/wiki/Insignia" title="Insignia">insignias</a>. It also reports that Breivik spent thousands of hours gathering email addresses from Facebook for distribution of the document, and that he rented a farm as a cover for a fake farming company buying <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer</a> (3 tons for producing explosives and 3 tons of a harmless kind to avoid suspicion) and as a lab. It describes burying a crate with the armour in the woods in July 2010, collecting it on 4 July 2011, and abandoning his plan to replace it with survival gear because he did not have a second pistol. It also expresses support for far-right groups such as the <a href="/wiki/English_Defence_League" title="English Defence League">English Defence League</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitaries</a> such as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scorpions_(Serbia)" title="Scorpions (Serbia)">Scorpions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the introductory chapter of the manifesto defining "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural_Marxism" title="Cultural Marxism">Cultural Marxism</a>" in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_School_conspiracy_theory" title="Frankfurt School conspiracy theory">Frankfurt School conspiracy theory</a> sense is a copy of <i>Political Correctness: A Short History of an Ideology</i> by the <a href="/wiki/Free_Congress_Foundation" title="Free Congress Foundation">Free Congress Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> Major parts of the compendium are attributed to the pseudonymous Norwegian blogger <a href="/wiki/Fjordman" title="Fjordman">Fjordman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> The text also copies sections of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unabomber_manifesto" title="Unabomber manifesto">Unabomber manifesto</a>, without giving credit, while replacing the words "leftists" with "cultural Marxists" and "black people" with "muslims".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> described American influences in the writings, noting that the compendium mentions the anti-Islamist American <a href="/wiki/Robert_Spencer_(author)" title="Robert Spencer (author)">Robert Spencer</a> 64 times and cites Spencer's works at great length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> The work of <a href="/wiki/Bat_Ye%27or" title="Bat Ye'or">Bat Ye'or</a> is frequently cited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neoconservative" title="Neoconservative">Neoconservative</a> blogger <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Geller" title="Pamela Geller">Pamela Geller</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Neo-pagan writer <a href="/wiki/Koenraad_Elst" title="Koenraad Elst">Koenraad Elst</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Pipes" title="Daniel Pipes">Daniel Pipes</a> are also mentioned as sources of inspiration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> The manifesto further contains quotes from <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">Thomas Jefferson</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Orwell" title="George Orwell">George Orwell</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melanie_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-melanie-216">[216]</a></sup> as well as from <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Clarkson" title="Jeremy Clarkson">Jeremy Clarkson</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sunday_Times" title="Sunday Times">Sunday Times</a></i> column and <a href="/wiki/Melanie_Phillips" title="Melanie Phillips">Melanie Phillips</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">Daily Mail</a></i> column.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> The publication speaks in admiration of <a href="/wiki/Ayaan_Hirsi_Ali" title="Ayaan Hirsi Ali">Ayaan Hirsi Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Bawer" title="Bruce Bawer">Bruce Bawer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sr%C4%91a_Trifkovi%C4%87" title="SrÄa TrifkoviÄ">SrÄa TrifkoviÄ</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henryk_M._Broder" title="Henryk M. Broder">Henryk M. Broder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> Breivik blames feminism for allowing the erosion of the fabric of European society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones20110727_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jones20110727-15">[15]</a></sup> The compendium advocates a restoration of <a href="/wiki/Patriarchy" title="Patriarchy">patriarchy</a> which it claims would save European culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones20110727_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-Jones20110727-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norway_Killer.27s_Hatred_of_Women_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norway_Killer.27s_Hatred_of_Women-220">[220]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his writings Breivik states that he wants to see European policies on <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a> and immigration more similar to those of Japan, South Korea and Taiwan<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-killer_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-killer-221">[221]</a></sup> which he said are "not far from cultural conservatism and nationalism at its best".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TeleD_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-TeleD-222">[222]</a></sup> He expressed his admiration for the "<a href="/wiki/Monoculturalism" title="Monoculturalism">monoculturalism</a>" of Japan and for the two nations' refusal to accept refugees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aso_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-Aso-224">[224]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jerusalem_Post" title="The Jerusalem Post">The Jerusalem Post</a></i> describes his support for Israel as a "far-right Zionism". He calls all "nationalists" to join in the struggle against "cultural Marxists/multiculturalists".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jpost-islamophobia_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-jpost-islamophobia-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>He also expressed his admiration of the Russian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, finding him "a fair and resolute leader worthy of respect", though he was "unsure at this point whether he has the potential to be our best friend or our worst enemy." Putin's spokesman Dmitri Peskov has denounced Breivik's actions as the "delirium of a madman".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis">Analysis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Analysis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_R._Teitelbaum" title="Benjamin R. Teitelbaum">Benjamin R. Teitelbaum</a>, Professor of Nordic Studies at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Colorado" title="University of Colorado">University of Colorado</a>, argues that several parts of the manifesto suggest that Breivik was concerned about race, not only about Western culture or Christianity, labelling him as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_nationalist" title="White nationalist">white nationalist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dagbladet1_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-dagbladet1-226">[226]</a></sup></p>
<p>Thomas Hegghammer of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Defence_Research_Establishment" title="Norwegian Defence Research Establishment">Norwegian Defence Research Establishment</a> has described the ideologies of Breivik as "not fitting the established categories of right-wing ideology, like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_supremacism" title="White supremacism">white supremacism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ultranationalism" title="Ultranationalism">ultranationalism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Christian_fundamentalism" title="Christian fundamentalism">Christian fundamentalism</a>", but more akin to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macro-nationalism" title="Macro-nationalism">macro-nationalism</a> and a "new doctrine of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clash_of_civilisations" title="Clash of civilisations">civilisational war</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Norwegian social scientist <a href="/wiki/Lars_Gule" title="Lars Gule">Lars Gule</a> characterised Breivik as a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_conservative" title="National conservative">national conservative</a>, not a Nazi".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> Pepe Egger of the think-tank Exclusive Analysis says "the bizarre thing is that his ideas, as Islamophobic as they are, are almost mainstream in many European countries".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup></p>
<p>In one section of the manifesto titled "Battlefield Wikipedia", Breivik explains the importance of using <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia" title="Wikipedia">Wikipedia</a> as a venue for disseminating views and information to the general public,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> although the Norwegian professor Arnulf Hagen claims that this was a document that he had copied from another author and that Breivik was unlikely to be a contributor to Wikipedia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> According to the leader of the Norwegian chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation" title="Wikimedia Foundation">Wikimedia Foundation</a> an account has been identified which they believe Breivik used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> On the second day of his trial Breivik cited Wikipedia as the main source for his worldview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wikipedia_234-0"><a href="#cite_note-wikipedia-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_and_political_views">Religious and political views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Religious and political views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamophobia">Islamophobia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Islamophobia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following his apprehension, Breivik was characterised by analysts as being a right-wing extremist with <a href="/wiki/Islamophobia" title="Islamophobia">anti-Muslim</a> views and a deep-seated hatred of Islam,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup> who considered himself a knight dedicated to stemming the tide of Muslim immigration into Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was at first described by many in the media as a <a href="/wiki/Christian_fundamentalism" title="Christian fundamentalism">Christian fundamentalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_terrorism" title="Christian terrorism">Christian terrorist</a>, and nationalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andresen_78-2"><a href="#cite_note-Andresen-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters1_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-at_least_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-at_least-239">[239]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juergensmeyer_242-0"><a href="#cite_note-Juergensmeyer-242">[242]</a></sup> He claims that the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> is a project to create "<a href="/wiki/Eurabia" title="Eurabia">Eurabia</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> and describes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia" title="1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia">1999 NATO bombing of Yugoslavia</a> as being authorised by "criminal western European and American leaders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> In his writings Breivik states that "the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Battle of Vienna</a> in 1683 should be celebrated as the Independence Day for all Western Europeans as it was the beginning of the end for the second Islamic wave of Jihads".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<p>The manifesto urges the Hindu nationalists to drive Muslims out of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> He demands the forced <a href="/wiki/Deportation" title="Deportation">deportation</a> of all Muslims from Europe, based on the model of the <a href="/wiki/Bene%C5%A1_decrees" title="BeneÅ¡ decrees">BeneÅ¡ decrees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-praguepost_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-praguepost-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>His religious faith is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odinism" title="Odinism">Odinism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagen191115_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Dagen191115-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogeneratedvl_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogeneratedvl-31">[31]</a></sup> but Breivik and others have previously linked his religious beliefs to Christianity.</p>
<p>The manifesto states its author is "100Â percent Christian",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Union_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Union-40">[40]</a></sup> but he is not "excessively religious";<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Union_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Union-40">[40]</a></sup> "I'm not going to pretend I'm a very religious person, as that would be a lie"; and considers himself a "<a href="/wiki/Cultural_Christian" title="Cultural Christian">cultural Christian</a>" and a "modern-day crusader".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_Union_40-3"><a href="#cite_note-Times_Union-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes0725_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes0725-250">[250]</a></sup> He calls religion a crutch and a source for drawing mental strength, and says "I've always been very pragmatic and influenced by my secular surroundings and environment". Regarding the term <i>cultural Christian</i>, which he says means preserving European culture, he notes, "It is enough that you are a Christian-agnostic or a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_atheist" title="Christian atheist">Christian-atheist</a> (an atheist who wants to preserve at least the basics of the European Christian cultural legacy...)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Juergensmeyer_242-1"><a href="#cite_note-Juergensmeyer-242">[242]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes0725_250-1"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes0725-250">[250]</a></sup> Furthermore, Breivik said "myself and many more like me do not necessarily have a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personal_relationship_with_Jesus_Christ" title="Personal relationship with Jesus Christ">personal relationship with Jesus Christ</a> and <a href="/wiki/God_in_Christianity" title="God in Christianity">God</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes0725_250-2"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes0725-250">[250]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Relationship2_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Relationship2-251">[251]</a></sup> Nevertheless, he said he planned to pray to God for help during his attacks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> Before the attacks, he stated an intention to attend <a href="/wiki/Frogner_Church" title="Frogner Church">Frogner Church</a> in a final "Martyr's mass".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik condemned <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> for his dialogue with Islam: "Pope Benedict has abandoned Christianity and all Christian Europeans and is to be considered a cowardly, incompetent, corrupt and illegitimate Pope." It will thus be necessary, writes Breivik, to overthrow the Protestant and Catholic hierarchies, after which a "Great Christian Congress" would set up a new European Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cesnur_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-cesnur-254">[254]</a></sup> He has also condemned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_(Christianity)" title="Mission (Christianity)">Christian missionary</a> activity in India as it would lead to the "total destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu faith</a> and culture", and he expresses support for the <a href="/wiki/Hindutva" title="Hindutva">Hindutva</a> movement against Indian Communist movements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hindu_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hindu-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2009, he wrote: "Today's Protestant church is a joke. Priests in jeans who march for Palestine and churches that look like minimalist shopping centres. I am a supporter of an indirect collective conversion of the Protestant church back to the Catholic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup></p>
<p>The American Christian press has suggested that Breivik also appears to have directly addressed followers of the neopagan religion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Odinism" title="Odinism">Odinism</a>, saying "even Odinists can fight with us or by our side as brothers" in the Knights Templar organisation of which Breivik claims to be a founding member. He later advocated rejecting Odinism, however, saying that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mjollnir" title="Mjollnir">Thor's Hammer</a> could not unify the people of Europe, but that the <a href="/wiki/Christian_cross" title="Christian cross">Christian cross</a> would.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<p>Deputy police chief <a href="/wiki/Roger_Andresen" title="Roger Andresen">Roger Andresen</a> initially told reporters that information on Breivik's websites was "so to speak, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundamentalist_Christianity" title="Fundamentalist Christianity">Christian fundamentalist</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andresen_78-3"><a href="#cite_note-Andresen-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webcache.googleusercontent.com_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-webcache.googleusercontent.com-258">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMH_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMH-259">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> and many mainstream media such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> have described him a Christian fundamentalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> Others, however, have disputed Andresen's characterisation of Breivik as a Christian fundamentalist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cesnur_254-1"><a href="#cite_note-cesnur-254">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brown_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-brown-262">[262]</a></sup></p>
<p>In letters sent to Norwegian newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Dagen_(Norwegian_newspaper)" title="Dagen (Norwegian newspaper)">Dagen</a></i> in 2015, Breivik said that he "is not, and has never been a Christian", and that he thinks there are few things in the world more "pathetic" than "the Jesus-figure and his message".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagen191115_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Dagen191115-29">[29]</a></sup> He said he prays and sacrifices to <a href="/wiki/Odin" title="Odin">Odin</a>, and identifies his religion as Odinism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dagen191115_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-Dagen191115-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Links_to_organizations">Links to organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Links to organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shooting_club">Shooting club</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Shooting club">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Breivik was an active member of an Oslo shooting club between 2005 and 2007, and since 2010. According to the club, which banned him for life after the attacks, Breivik had taken part in 13 organized training sessions and one competition since June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> The club states that it does not evaluate the members' suitability regarding possession of weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Freemasons">Freemasons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Freemasons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the time of the attacks, Breivik was a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masonic_Lodge" title="Masonic Lodge">Lodge</a> of St. Olaf at the Three Columns in Oslo<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> and had displayed photographs of himself in partial Masonic regalia on his Facebook profile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> In interviews after the attacks, his lodge said it had only minimal contact with him, and that when made aware of Breivik's membership, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_(Masonic)" title="Grand Master (Masonic)">Grand Master</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Order_of_Freemasons" title="Norwegian Order of Freemasons">Norwegian Order of Freemasons</a>, Ivar A. Skaar, issued an edict immediately excluding him from the fraternity based upon the acts he carried out and the values that appear to have motivated them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup> According to the Lodge records, Breivik took part in a total of four meetings between his initiation in February 2007 and his exclusion from the order â one each to receive the first, second and third degree, and one other meeting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-270">[270]</a></sup> and held no offices or functions within the Lodge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> Skaar said that although Breivik was a member of the Order, his actions showed that he is in no way a Mason.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_270-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-270">[270]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Progress_Party">Progress Party</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Progress Party">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Breivik became a member of the <a href="/wiki/Progress_Party_(Norway)" title="Progress Party (Norway)">Progress Party</a> (FrP) in 1999. He paid his membership dues for the last time in 2004, and was removed from the membership lists in 2006.</p>
<p>During his time in the Progress Party, he held two positions in the Progress Party's youth organisation FpU: he was the chair of the local Vest Oslo branch from January to October 2002, and a member of the board of the same branch from October 2002 till November 2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AP-brv_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-AP-brv-272">[272]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBeaumont_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBeaumont-273">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the attack, the Progress Party immediately distanced itself from Breivik's actions and ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TB-brv_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-TB-brv-275">[275]</a></sup> At a 2013 press conference <a href="/wiki/Ketil_Solvik-Olsen" title="Ketil Solvik-Olsen">Ketil Solvik-Olsen</a> said that Breivik "left us [the party] because we were too liberal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="English_Defence_League_.28EDL.29">English Defence League (EDL)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: English Defence League (EDL)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Breivik claimed he had contact with the far-right <a href="/wiki/English_Defence_League" title="English Defence League">English Defence League</a> (EDL), a movement in the United Kingdom that has been accused of Islamophobia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Craig_Murray_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-Craig_Murray-277">[277]</a></sup> He allegedly had extensive links with senior EDL members<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup> and wrote that he attended an EDL demonstration in <a href="/wiki/Bradford" title="Bradford">Bradford</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> On 26 July 2011, EDL leader <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Yaxley-Lennon" title="Stephen Yaxley-Lennon">Tommy Robinson</a> denounced Breivik and his attacks and has denied any official links with him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BigJay_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-BigJay-280">[280]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 July 2011, <a href="/wiki/Interpol" title="Interpol">Interpol</a> asked Maltese police to investigate Paul Ray, a former EDL member who blogs under the name "Lionheart." Ray conceded that he may have been an inspiration for Breivik, but deplored his actions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an online discussion on the Norwegian website <a href="/wiki/Document.no" title="Document.no">Document.no</a> on 6 December 2009, Breivik proposes to establish a Norwegian version of the EDL. Breivik saw this as the only way to stop left-wing radical groups like <a href="/wiki/Blitz_(movement)" title="Blitz (movement)">Blitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/SOS_Rasisme" title="SOS Rasisme">SOS Rasisme</a> from "harassing" Norwegian cultural conservatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> Following the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/European_Defence_League" title="European Defence League">European Defence League</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_Defence_League" title="Norwegian Defence League">Norwegian Defence League</a> (NDL) launched in 2010. Breivik indeed became a member of this organization under the pseudonym "<a href="/wiki/Sigurd_the_Crusader" title="Sigurd the Crusader">Sigurd Jorsalfar</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> Former head of the NDL, Lena Andreassen, claims that Breivik was ejected from the organization when she took over as leader in March 2011 because he was too extreme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Knights_Templar">Knights Templar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Knights Templar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar_and_popular_culture" title="Knights Templar and popular culture">Knights Templar and popular culture</a></div>
<p>In his manifesto and during interrogation, Breivik claimed membership in an "international Christian military order", which he calls the new <i>Pauperes commilitones Christi Templique Solomonici</i> (PCCTS, <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Knights Templar</a>). According to Breivik, the order was established as an "anti-<a href="/wiki/Jihad" title="Jihad">Jihad</a> crusader-organisation" that "fights" against "Islamic suppression" in London in April 2002 by nine men: two Englishmen, a Frenchman, a German, a Dutchman, a Greek, a Russian, a Norwegian (apparently Breivik), and a Serb (supposedly the initiator, not present, but represented by Breivik). The compendium gives a "2008 estimate" that there are between 15 and 80 "Justiciar Knights" in Western Europe, and an unknown number of civilian members, and Breivik expects the order to take political and military control of Western Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik gives his own code name in the organisation as Sigurd and that of his assigned "mentor" as Richard, after the twelfth-century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crusaders" title="Crusaders">crusaders</a> and kings <a href="/wiki/Sigurd_the_Crusader" title="Sigurd the Crusader">Sigurd Jorsalfar</a> of Norway and <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard the Lionheart</a> of England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-db1_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-db1-287">[287]</a></sup> He calls himself a one-man <a href="/wiki/Clandestine_cell_system" title="Clandestine cell system">cell</a> of this organisation, and claims that the group has several other cells in Western countries, including two more in Norway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Haaretz1_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-Haaretz1-88">[88]</a></sup> On 2 August 2011 Breivik offered to provide information about these cells, but on unrealistic preconditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup></p>
<p>After an intense investigation assisted internationally by several <a href="/wiki/Security_agency" title="Security agency">security agencies</a>, the Norwegian police have not found any evidence that a PCCTS network existed, or that the alleged 2002 London meeting ever took place. The police now view Breivik's claim as a figment of imagination in light of his schizophrenia diagnosis, and are increasingly confident that he had no <a href="/wiki/Accessory_(legal_term)" title="Accessory (legal term)">accessories</a>. The perpetrator still insists he belongs to an order and that his one-man cell was "activated" by another clandestine cell.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 August 2012, several Norwegian politicians and media outlets received an email from someone claiming to be Breivik's "deputy", demanding that Breivik be released, and making more threats against Norwegian society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Intellectual_influences">Intellectual influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Intellectual influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Breivik has identified himself in a multitude of <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a> services as an admirer of, among others, the <a href="/wiki/Freedom_Party_of_Austria" title="Freedom Party of Austria">Freedom Party of Austria</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hindu_nationalism" title="Hindu nationalism">Hindu nationalism</a> (<i>Hindutva</i>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> the right-wing <a href="/wiki/Swiss_People%27s_Party" title="Swiss People's Party">Swiss People's Party</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elmundo_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-elmundo-295">[295]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Max_Manus" title="Max Manus">Max Manus</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-webcache.googleusercontent.com_258-1"><a href="#cite_note-webcache.googleusercontent.com-258">[258]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elmundo_295-1"><a href="#cite_note-elmundo-295">[295]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Robert_Spencer_(writer)" title="Robert Spencer (writer)">Robert Spencer</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-296">[296]</a></sup> former Japanese Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taro_Aso" title="Taro Aso">Taro Aso</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aso_224-1"><a href="#cite_note-Aso-224">[224]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrick_Buchanan" title="Patrick Buchanan">Patrick Buchanan</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norway_Killer.27s_Hatred_of_Women_220-1"><a href="#cite_note-Norway_Killer.27s_Hatred_of_Women-220">[220]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ayaan_Hirsi_Ali" title="Ayaan Hirsi Ali">Ayaan Hirsi Ali</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Radovan_Karad%C5%BEi%C4%87" title="Radovan KaradÅ¾iÄ">Radovan KaradÅ¾iÄ</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sr%C4%91a_Trifkovi%C4%87" title="SrÄa TrifkoviÄ">SrÄa TrifkoviÄ</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> and Dutch politician <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Party_for_Freedom" title="Party for Freedom">whose political party</a> he described on the website of the periodical <i><a href="/wiki/Minerva_(Norwegian_periodical)" title="Minerva (Norwegian periodical)">Minerva</a></i> as one among the few that could "truly claim to be conservative parties in their whole culture." Wilders quickly distanced himself from Breivik and denounced him as "violent and sick".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> On Twitter, he paraphrased philosopher <a href="/wiki/John_Stuart_Mill" title="John Stuart Mill">John Stuart Mill</a>: "One person with a belief is equal to the force of 100,000 who have only interests".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VG-perp_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-VG-perp-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> Breivik had been active on several anti-Islamic and nationalist blogs, including <i><a href="/wiki/Document.no" title="Document.no">document.no</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> and was a regular reader of <i>Gates of Vienna</i>, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brussels_Journal" title="Brussels Journal">Brussels Journal</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Jihad_Watch" title="Jihad Watch">Jihad Watch</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup></p>
<p>Breivik has frequently praised the writings of blogger <a href="/wiki/Fjordman" title="Fjordman">Fjordman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> He used Fjordman's thinking to justify his actions, citing him 111 times in the manifesto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> He also endorsed the writings of Australian historian <a href="/wiki/Keith_Windschuttle" title="Keith Windschuttle">Keith Windschuttle</a> in the manifesto <i>2083</i>, as well as former Australian Prime Minister John Howard and former Czech President <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Klaus" title="VÃ¡clav Klaus">VÃ¡clav Klaus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nz_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-nz-306">[306]</a></sup> He expressed admiration for historical military leaders such as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Martel" title="Charles Martel">Charles Martel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_I_of_England" title="Richard I of England">Richard the Lionheart</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">El Cid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlad_the_Impaler" title="Vlad the Impaler">Vlad the Impaler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jacques_de_Molay" title="Jacques de Molay">Jacques de Molay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_I_of_Russia" title="Nicholas I of Russia">Nicholas I of Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Hunyadi" title="John Hunyadi">John Hunyadi</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">John III Sobieski</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> In his manifest he copies 25 pages verbatim from an ideological text by <a href="/wiki/Evan_Kohlmann" title="Evan Kohlmann">Evan Kohlmann</a> and published by an institute led by <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Ranstorp" title="Magnus Ranstorp">Magnus Ranstorp</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup></p>
<p>After studying several militant groups, including <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republican_Army" title="Irish Republican Army">IRA</a>, <a href="/wiki/ETA_(separatist_group)" title="ETA (separatist group)">ETA</a> and others, Breivik suggests far-right militants should adopt <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a>'s methods, learn from their success, and avoid their mistakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> Breivik described al-Qaeda as the "most successful revolutionary force in the world" and praised their "cult of martyrdom".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wikipedia_234-1"><a href="#cite_note-wikipedia-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a letter sent by Breivik to international media in January 2014, Breivik states that he exploited "counterjihadist" rhetoric in order to protect "ethno-nationalists" and start a media hunt against "anti-nationalist counterjihadist"-supporters, in a strategy he calls "double psychology". Breivik further states that he strives for a "pure Nordic ideal", advocating the establishment of a similar party in Norway to the (now-defunct) <a href="/wiki/Neo-Nazism" title="Neo-Nazism">neo-Nazi</a> <a href="/wiki/Party_of_the_Swedes" title="Party of the Swedes">Party of the Swedes</a>, and identifying himself as a part of "Western Europe's <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> movement". Moreover, he states that his "support" for Israel is limited for it to function as a place to deport "disloyal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">Jews</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Expo14_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Expo14-30">[30]</a></sup> During the trial in 2012, Breivik listed as his influences a number of neo-Nazi activists, as well as perpetrators of attacks against immigrants and leftists, considering them "heroes".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_related_books">Notable related books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Notable related books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 17 August 2013, journalist <a href="/wiki/Marit_Christensen" title="Marit Christensen">Marit Christensen</a> informed the Norwegian press that for the last year of Wenche Behring Breivik's life, she had been her confidant, and that a book based on Christensen's interviews with her would be published as a book in late 2013 under the title <i>The Mother</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> On 14 September 2013 <a href="/wiki/Verdens_Gang" title="Verdens Gang">Verdens Gang</a> said that before Wenche Behring Breivik died, she hired a lawyer to prevent<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stop-publishing_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stop-publishing-314">[314]</a></sup> Christensen from publishing the book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deathbed_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deathbed-315">[315]</a></sup> The book was nevertheless published in October 2013, and was widely criticized; on the basis of Wenche Behring Breivik's opposition to the book, for inclusion of material not relevant to understanding what motivated Anders Behring Breivik, and for character assassinations of still living people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tyrannical_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tyrannical-316">[316]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Anders_Behring_Breivik&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>In January 2012 the Danish theatre <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Teatret" title="CafÃ© Teatret">CafÃ© Teatret</a> announced that it was staging a play based on the manifesto. The play, named <i>Manifesto 2083</i> was planned to be performed over three weeks in August 2012. Relatives of the victims of Breivik's actions as well as Danish politicians have criticized the plans of the theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> In February 2012 the Norwegian Dramatikkens Hus announced it too will be staging the Danish play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> Three weeks into Breivik's criminal trial the producer of the play, Christian Lollike, announced that the play has been postponed indefinitely. Lollike cited the ongoing trial as the reason for the decision in that much of what was intended to be discussed in the play has been illuminated through the trial proceedings: "Of course, if we feel that we have nothing interesting to say in relation to this case we will drop the performance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup></li>
<li>Another play was premiered in Amsterdam, on 22 March. The play <i>Breivik meets Wilders</i> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <span lang="nl"><i>Breivik ontmoet Wilders</i></span>) depicts a fictional meeting between Anders Behring Breivik and controversial Dutch lawmaker <a href="/wiki/Geert_Wilders" title="Geert Wilders">Geert Wilders</a> at London's Heathrow airport in March 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> The play, running at Amsterdam's <a href="/wiki/De_Balie" title="De Balie">De Balie</a> theatre is written by playwright <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Holman" title="Theodor Holman">Theodor Holman</a> who one week ahead of the premiere said "I feel a kinship with Anders Breivik."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> Other plays are currently under development in Sweden and the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322">[322]</a></sup></li>
<li>The German clothing chain <a href="/wiki/Thor_Steinar" title="Thor Steinar">Thor Steinar</a>, which names all its shops after Norwegian towns, has had two stores named <i>Brevik</i>, after the Norwegian town <a href="/wiki/Brevik" title="Brevik">Brevik</a> in <a href="/wiki/Telemark" title="Telemark">Telemark</a>. The first closed in 2008, and a new one opened in <a href="/wiki/Chemnitz" title="Chemnitz">Chemnitz</a> in February 2012. The similarity of the name Brevik to Breivik's name led to vandalism when the new Brevik store opened, forcing it to change its name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323">[323]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cecilie_L%C3%B8veid" title="Cecilie LÃ¸veid">Cecilie LÃ¸veid</a>'s poem "Punishment" (<i>Straff</i>) was printed in <i><a href="/wiki/Aftenposten" title="Aftenposten">Aftenposten</a></i>, as "This Week's Poem", on 8 April 2013. In an interview with the newspaper, she said that the poem is about Breivik, and that she has no opinion about the verdict of the trialâbecause that is outside the scope of the poem.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the 2013 documentary film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pervert%27s_Guide_to_Ideology" title="The Pervert's Guide to Ideology">The Pervert's Guide to Ideology</a></i>, Slovene philosopher and psychoanalyst <a href="/wiki/Slavoj_%C5%BDi%C5%BEek" title="Slavoj Å½iÅ¾ek">Slavoj Å½iÅ¾ek</a>, in discussing the meaning of ideology in modern life, compares the mind-set and actions of Breivik to examples from popular culture, in particular the thoughts and actions of Travis Bickle (Robert De Niro) in the 1976 film <i><a href="/wiki/Taxi_Driver" title="Taxi Driver">Taxi Driver</a></i>, whereby he first analyses in his own mind the problems of his environment (New York streets controlled by pimps and drug dealers) but then attempts to resolve them through an act of great violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>The 2012 play ["the martyrs"] <i>MÃ¤rtyrer</i> by <a href="/wiki/Marius_von_Mayenburg" title="Marius von Mayenburg">Marius von Mayenburg</a>, as opined by the play's director (Anders T. Andersen) at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationaltheatret" title="Nationaltheatret">Nationaltheatret</a>, [is about that] "it's obvious that the actions of Anders Behring Breivik on 22 July 2011 were motivated by Christianity and it is striking that the term, Christian terrorism barely exists. ... Regarding Breivik, our trick has been to split him (into two [entities]). On the one hand we have recognised him as sane, to be able to punish him, something which was important to us as a nation. On the other hand we relate to him as a lunatic, so that we can be spared from having to relate to him as a Norwegianâone of us".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup></p>

(...) RegissÃ¸ren mener det er Ã¥penbart at Anders Behring Breiviks handlinger 22. juli 2011 var motivert av kristendommen og at det er pÃ¥fallende at begrepet kristen-terrorisme knapt eksisterer. (...) Med Breivik har vi gjort det kunststykket Ã¥ dele ham i to. PÃ¥ den ene sida har vi erkjent ham tilregnelig for Ã¥ kunne straffe ham, noe som var viktig for oss som nasjon.
